No Two Proximate Differentiae for One Species
Author proves a single species cannot have two proximate differentiae.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a single species cannot have two proximate differentiae and identify the logical consequence of attempting such a definition.

Core Idea
One species, one differentia: two differentiae collapse into one or cause redundancy.

This passage from the logic tradition establishes a key principle of definition: a species can have only one proximate differentia. The proof is elegant, drawing on the analogy of causes and effects. We will walk through the reasoning step by step to understand why this rule holds and what happens if it is violated.

Guided Path
1
Understand the rule
The author states the rule clearly: 'ولا يكون لشيء واحد فصلان قريبان' — there cannot be two proximate differentiae for one thing. This is the claim we need to analyze.
The 'thing' here refers to a species, meaning the lowest genus under which individuals fall.
2
Identify the consequence if violated
The author warns that if two differentiae existed, it would entail 'توارد العلل المستقلة على معلول واحد' — the concurrence of independent causes upon one effect, which is impossible. This is the logical consequence used as a proof.
In logic, one effect cannot have two independent complete causes; similarly, one species cannot have two independent defining differentiae.
3
Analyze the two scenarios
The proof splits into two cases. First, if each differentia alone suffices to give the species its specific existence (تحصل), then one is redundant, leading to 'الاستغناء عن الذاتي' (independence from the essential). Second, if neither alone suffices, then their combination effectively becomes a single differentia.
Thus, in either case, you cannot have two truly independent differentiae.
4
Check the condition
The author notes that this reasoning depends on defining 'differentia' as 'المميز التام' — the complete distinguisher. If the differentia is defined differently (e.g., as any distinguishing feature), the argument may not hold. This highlights the importance of precise definitions in logic.
Understanding this condition prevents misapplication of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يكون لشيء واحد فصلان قريبان، وإلا يلزم توارد العلل المستقلة على معلول واحد، وإن كان في إعطاء التحصل، وربما يقرر بأنه إن كفى كل منهما في تحصله نوعا فيلزم الاستغناء عن الذاتي، وإلا فيكون مجموعهما فصلا واحدا وهذا إنما يتم لو كان الفصل عبارة عن المميز التام، وإلا فلا يخفى ما فيه.
And there cannot be for one thing two proximate differentiae; otherwise there would occur the concurrence of independent causes upon one effect, even if it is in giving specific existence. And perhaps it is established that if each of them suffices for its specific existence as a species, then independence from the essential would follow; otherwise their sum would be one differentia. This is only valid if the differentia is the complete distinguisher; otherwise what is in it is not hidden.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage states a logical rule: a single thing (meaning a species) cannot have two proximate differentiae. The proof is that two differentiae would be like two independent causes producing one effect, which is impossible. The commentary further explains: if each differentia alone were sufficient to define the species, then the other would be redundant; if neither alone is sufficient, then their combination is actually a single differentia. This reasoning depends on the definition of differentia as the complete distinguisher (المميز التام). If differentia is defined differently, the argument may not hold.

Key Terms

توارد العلل المستقلة

Key Takeaway
A species cannot have two proximate differentiae because they would either be redundant or combine into one, analogous to the impossibility of two independent causes for one effect.

Two Rules of the Differentia
Author states two rules: differentia constitutes only one species and is only accompanied by one genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the two rules of the differentia to determine whether a given definition yields a real or relational species.

Core Idea
A differentia can only constitute one species and pair with one genus, or the species becomes relational not real.

In this concise passage, the author lays down two essential rules that govern the use of differentiae in definitions. These rules ensure that when we define a species using its genus and differentia, the result is a genuine, real species (naw' haqiqi) rather than a merely relational one (naw' i'tibari). Understanding these rules is critical for constructing sound definitions in any Islamic science, from fiqh to kalam.

Guided Path
1
Locate the two rules
Read the first sentence: the differentia constitutes only one species unless it is relational. Then the second: it is accompanied by only one genus. These are the two core principles.
2
Distinguish real vs. relational
A real differentia (not i'tibari) gives a real species. A relational differentia could be a cause for two genera, but that would not produce a real species. Notice the condition 'if it is not relational'.
The term 'i'tibari' is crucial – it means 'relational' or 'considered-as', not essential.
3
Test with an example
Take 'rational' as a differentia. It constitutes only one real species: 'human'. It cannot constitute 'animal' as a species because 'animal' is a genus. Moreover, 'rational' is accompanied by only one genus (e.g., 'animal') in the definition 'rational animal'. If paired with both 'animal' and 'living body', the species would be relational.
4
Apply to a definition from fiqh
Consider the definition of 'riba al-nasi'ah' as 'an exchange with deferment where the deferment is the differentia'. Check: Does 'deferment' constitute only one species of riba? Does it pair with only one genus (e.g., 'exchange')? If it could also constitute another species with another genus, the definition would be flawed.
This helps validate definitions in usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقوم الفصل إلا نوعا واحدا، إذا لم يكن اعتباريا، وإلا لكان الشيء علة لأمرين، وهما جنساه، ولا يقارن إلا جنسا واحدا، فيحصله نوعا حقيقيا غير اعتباري لما مر.
And the differentia constitutes only one species, if it is not relational; otherwise the thing would be a cause for two things, which are its two genera. And it is only accompanied by one genus, thus it actualizes a real species, not a relational one, according to what has passed.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage presents two rules about the differentia. First, a differentia constitutes only one species (i.e., it is the specific difference for only one species) unless it is a relational (اعتباري) differentia, in which case it could be a cause for two genera. Second, a differentia is accompanied by only one genus in a real definition, meaning that in the hierarchy of genera, the differentia is paired with the proximate genus to form a species. If it were accompanied by more than one genus, the species would not be real but relational. This ensures that the definition (hadd) is proper.

Key Terms
يقوم
اعتباري
يقارن
نوع حقيقي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) No, because a differentia constitutes only one species.
C) Yes, if 'animal' is a broader category.
D) No, because 'animal' is a genus, not a species.

Key Takeaway
The differentia must constitute exactly one real species and pair with exactly one genus, otherwise the species is relational not real.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Peripatetic Argument: Differentia of Substance Must Be Substance
Peripatetic argument against accidental differentia

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the Peripatetic conditional argument that the differentia of substance cannot be an accident.

Core Idea
If the differentia of a substance were an accident, the effect would be stronger than its cause — an impossibility.

The Peripatetics (Aristotelians) argued that the differentia (fasl) of a substance must itself be a substance. Their reasoning hinged on a causal principle: the cause must be at least as strong as its effect. In this lesson, we will break down their conditional argument and see why an accidental differentia would violate that principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
The Peripatetics assert that the differentia of substance is substance. Find this statement in the Arabic: 'وفصل الجوهر جوهر'.
The claim is the opening of the passage.
2
Extract the conditional premise
The author presents a conditional: 'وإلا لكان المعلول أقوى من العلة' — if the differentia were an accident, then the effect (the species) would be stronger than the cause (the differentia). Write this as an 'if...then' statement.
The conditional is implicit: 'If the differentia is an accident, then the effect is stronger than the cause.'
3
Identify the unstated premise
The argument relies on the principle that a cause must be stronger than or equal to its effect. Here, the cause (differentia) would be an accident, which is weaker than a substance. So the effect (substance) would be stronger—impossible. State this principle explicitly.
This is a modal principle often accepted in Aristotelian metaphysics.
4
Validate the modus tollens
The argument is a modus tollens: If P (differentia is accident) then Q (effect stronger than cause). Not-Q (effect not stronger than cause). Therefore, not-P. Confirm that the denial of the consequent leads to the denial of the antecedent.
This is a valid conditional syllogism (qiyas istithna'i).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفصل الجوهر جوهر، وإلا لكان المعلول أقوى من العلة، والعرض مبهم محتاج في تحصله إلى الغير، فكيف يكون مقوما، خلافا للإشراقية). اعلم أنهم قالوا الصور النوعية للجواهر أعراض، وقد تقدم أن الصور تكون فصولا ، فيلزمهم القول بعرضية الفصل ، ولذا نسب إليهم ، وإلا فهم لم يصرحوا بذلك . ثم اعلم أن الحق مع الإشراقية ؛ فإن مواد المركبات العنصرية غير محتاجة إلى صورها كيف ومحال صورها ليست إلا العناصر الأربعة الباقية الصور الموجودة بدونها، والحال لا يكون جوهرا إلا إذا احتاج المحل إليه ، ولم يقولوا بعلية الفصل للجنس ؛ حتى يلزم كونها أضعف منه ، بل قالوا للجزء الأخص فصلا ، والأعم جنسا، سواء كان الأخص مقوما له أو مقوما منه . والمشاؤون قالوا: إذا كان الأعم مقوما للأخص لا يلتئم منهما ماهية حقيقية ، وذلك مما لا دليل عليه، هذا والله أعلم بالصواب.
And the differentia of substance is substance, otherwise the effect would be stronger than the cause, and the accident is ambiguous, needing the other for its actualization, so how can it be constitutive? Contrary to the Ishraaqiyyun. Know that they said the specific forms of substances are accidents, and it has preceded that forms are differentiae, so it follows that they must say the differentia is accidental, so it is attributed to them, otherwise they did not explicitly say that. Then know that the truth is with the Ishraaqiyyun; for the materials of elemental composites do not need their forms, how so? And the forms of their atoms are only the remaining four elements that exist without them, and a state is not a substance unless the substrate needs it. And they did not say that the differentia is a cause for the genus such that it would be weaker than it, rather they said the more specific part is a differentia and the more general is a genus, whether the more specific is constitutive of it or constituted from it. And the Peripatetics said: if the more general is constitutive of the more specific, a real quiddity cannot be composed from them, but there is no proof for that. This, and God knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage argues that the differentia of a substance must itself be a substance, not an accident. The author first presents the Peripatetic argument: if the differentia were an accident, then the effect (the species) would be stronger than its cause (the differentia), which is impossible. The Ishraaqiyyun (Illuminationists) are said to hold that specific forms are accidents, hence the differentia would be accidental. The author then clarifies that the Ishraaqiyyun did not explicitly claim that, but it follows from their position. Surprisingly, the author then states that the truth is with the Ishraaqiyyun, offering a different perspective: elemental composites do not need their forms, and the forms of their atoms are just the four elements. They reject the notion of the differentia being a cause of the genus; instead, they simply define the more specific part as differentia and the more general as genus. The Peripatetics claim that if the more general is constitutive of the more specific, no real quiddity results, but the author says there is no proof for this. The passage ends with a traditional deferral to God's knowledge.

المعلول
العلة
العرض
مقوم

Checkpoint
Why does the Peripatetic argument claim the differentia of substance cannot be an accident?
A) Because accidents are weaker than substances.
B) Because an accident cannot cause a substance to be a substance.
C) Because the differentia is a cause of the species, and an accident is weaker than a substance, so the effect would be stronger than the cause.
D) Because all differentiae are substances by definition.

Key Takeaway
The Peripatetics used a modus tollens to prove that the differentia of substance must be substance, based on the causal principle that an effect cannot be stronger than its cause.

The Author's Critique: Truth with the Ishraaqiyyun
Author's critique of Peripatetics and defense of Ishraaqiyyun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's critique of the Peripatetic position and explain why he ultimately sides with the Ishraaqiyyun.

Core Idea
The differentia need not be a cause of the genus; a simpler account of species and genus suffices.

After presenting the Peripatetic argument, the author makes a surprising turn: 'the truth is with the Ishraaqiyyun.' He argues that the Peripatetic claim lacks proof, and the Ishraaqiyyun offer a more parsimonious account where the differentia is simply the more specific part, not necessarily constitutive of the genus. This lesson unpacks that critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Peripatetic target
The Peripatetics claimed that if the genus is constitutive of the species, no real quiddity results (if the more general is constitutive of the more specific, a real essence cannot be formed). Find this claim in the Arabic: 'إذا كان الأعم مقوما للأخص لا يلتئم منهما ماهية حقيقية'.
This is the claim the author rejects.
2
Extract the author's objection
The author states that there is no proof (دليل) for the Peripatetic position. He then offers an alternative view from the Ishraaqiyyun: they define the more specific part as the differentia and the more general as the genus, regardless of which is constitutive of which.
The Ishraaqiyyun do not require the differentia to be a cause of the genus.
3
Understand the Ishraaqiyyun's argument
The author explains that the Ishraaqiyyun say the materials of elemental composites do not need their forms, and the differentia is not a cause of the genus. They simply identify the more specific part as differentia and the more general as genus, without a causal relation.
This avoids the problem of the effect being stronger than the cause.
4
Evaluate the critique
The author's critique is that the Peripatetics have no evidence for their claim that genus must be constitutive. The Ishraaqiyyun offer a viable alternative that does not require that assumption. Assess whether the critique is logically sound: the author points out a lack of proof, which is a valid objection in dialectical reasoning.
The author does not fully endorse the Ishraaqiyyun view, but says the truth is with them on this point.

The Differentia of Substance: Peripatetic vs. Illuminationist Views
Author critiques the Mashsha'i claim that the differentia of substance is substance and defends the Ishraqi position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the Peripatetic argument that the differentia of substance must be substance and evaluate the Illuminationist critique of that argument.

Core Idea
The differentia need not be a cause of the genus; the Illuminationists redefine genus and differentia based on generality.

In classical logic, the differentia (fasl) is the specific difference that distinguishes a species from its genus. A key debate concerns whether the differentia of substance must itself be substance. Peripatetic philosophers argue yes, on causal grounds. The Illuminationist school (Ishraqiyyun) challenges this, claiming the differentia can be an accident. This lesson dissects both positions and their underlying assumptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Peripatetic thesis
Locate the statement: 'وفصل الجوهر جوهر' (And the differentia of substance is substance). This is the claim under debate.
The Peripatetics assert that the differentia must share the same category as the definiendum.
2
Extract the Peripatetic argument
The text provides a causal argument: if the differentia were an accident, the effect would be stronger than the cause, and an accident cannot be constitutive. Understand the logic: the differentia is supposed to be constitutive, but accidents depend on substance; hence the differentia must itself be substance.
The argument relies on the idea that the differentia is a cause of the species.
3
Understand the Illuminationist position
The Ishraqiyyun hold that the specific forms of substances are accidents, and forms serve as differentiate. This leads to the accusation that they consider the differentia accidental. But the text clarifies they did not explicitly say that.
The accusation is attributed to them by opponents, not necessarily their own view.
4
Analyze the Illuminationist defense
The author defends the Ishraqi view: they did not claim the differentia is a cause of the genus; rather, they define the more specific part as the differentia and the more general as the genus, regardless of which is constitutive. This avoids the causal objection.
The redefinition shifts the basis from causation to logical generality.
5
Evaluate the conclusion
The author sides with the Ishraqiyyun because the Peripatetics have no proof that a real essence cannot be formed from a more general constitutive part and a specific part. Determine if this critique is convincing.
The burden of proof is on the Peripatetics to show the impossibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الكليات الخمس نوعا حقيقيا غير اعتباري لما مر . ( وَفَصْلُ الْجَوْهَر جَوْهَرٌ ، وإلا لكان المعلول أقوى من العلة، والعرض مبهم محتاج في تحصله إلى الغير، فكيف يكون مقوما، خِلَافًا لِلْإِشْرَاقِيَّةِ). اعلم أنهم قالوا الصور النوعية للجواهر أعراض، وقد تقدم أن الصور تكون فصولا ، فيلزمهم القول بعرضية الفصل ، ولذا نسب إليهم ، وإلا فهم لم يصرحوا بذلك . ثم اعلم أن الحق مع الإشراقية ؛ فإن مواد المركبات العنصرية غير محتاجة إلى صورها كيف ومحال صورها ليست إلا العناصر الأربعة الباقية الصور الموجودة بدونها، والحال لا يكون جوهرا إلا إذا احتاج المحل إليه ، ولم يقولوا بعلية الفصل للجنس ؛ حتى يلزم كونها أضعف منه ، بل قالوا للجزء الأخص فصلا ، والأعم جنسا، سواء كان الأخص مقوما له أو مقوما منه . والمشاؤون قالوا: إذا كان الأعم مقوما للأخص لا يلتئم منهما ماهية حقيقية ، وذلك مما لا دليل عليه، هذا والله أعلم بالصواب.
Chapter on the five universals. A real type, not relative, as previously. And the differentia of substance is substance, otherwise the effect would be stronger than the cause, and the accident is ambiguous, needing another in its realization, so how can it be constitutive? Contrary to the Ishraqiyyun. Know that they said the specific forms of substances are accidents, and it has been established that forms are differentiate, so it follows that they claim that the differentia is accidental, and thus it is attributed to them; otherwise they did not explicitly state that. Then know that the truth is with the Ishraqiyyun; for the materials of elemental compounds do not need their forms, how so? And the loci of their forms are none other than the four elements that remain, existing without them, and the state is not substance unless the locus needs it. And they did not claim that the differentia is a cause of the genus, so that it would be weaker than it; rather they said that the more specific part is the differentia, and the more general is the genus, whether the specific is constitutive of it or constitutive from it. And the Peripatetics said: if the more general is constitutive of the specific, a real essence will not be composed from them, and there is no proof for that. This, and God knows best the truth.

Commentary
This passage is a definitional discussion about the nature of the differentia (fasl) in the context of the five universals. The author begins by restating the Peripatetic position that the differentia of substance must itself be substance, based on the argument that if it were accidental, the effect would be stronger than the cause and an accident cannot be constitutive. However, the author defends the Ishraqiyyun, arguing that they do not actually claim that the differentia is a cause of the genus, nor that its being an accident undermines its status. Rather, they simply define the more specific part as the differentia and the more general as the genus, regardless of which is constitutive. The Peripatetics' objection that a real essence cannot be composed from a more general constitutive part and a specific part is rejected as being without proof. The author concludes that the truth lies with the Ishraqiyyun on this point.

The Doubt of Multiple Differentiae from Uniform Universal Application
Author presents a doubt that a universal applies to many individuals with one application, leading to multiple proximate differentiae.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the doubt that a universal can have multiple proximate differentiae and identify its logical consequence.

Core Idea
A universal applies uniformly to many individuals, potentially forcing multiple differentiae for a single genus.

This passage presents a doubt from al-Dawani's Hashiya about the five universals. It challenges the standard view that each species has only one proximate differentia. By examining the universal 'animal' as it applies to both human and horse, the author shows that the sum of these species would require two differentiae (rational and neighing), which seems problematic. The objection that follows is incomplete in our text, but the doubt itself is a critical probe.

Guided Path
1
Identify the doubt
The doubt states that a universal applies to many individuals with a single application. That is, 'animal' applies to both human and horse in the same way.
This is not a claim about the universal's meaning but about its extension.
2
Apply to the example
Take the universal 'animal'. It applies to human and to horse. Therefore, the aggregate 'human + horse' is also animal.
The phrase "مجموع الإنسان والفرس حيوان" means the sum is animal, not that each is a different species separately.
3
Draw the consequence
If the sum is animal, then it must have a differentia that distinguishes this aggregate from other animals. But human and horse have different differentiae: rational and neighing. So the aggregate would have two differentiae.
This violates the principle that a species has only one proximate differentia.
4
Recognize the problem
The doubt reveals a tension: either the universal does not apply uniformly, or the sum can have multiple differentiae. Both options challenge classical definition theory.
The full objection and response are not present in this excerpt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالثَّانِي: مَا سَنَحَ لِي، وَهُوَ أَنَّ الْكُلِّيَّ كَمَا يَصْدُقُ عَلَى وَاحِدٍ مِنْ أَفْرَادِهِ يَصْدُقُ عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ مِنْ أَفْرَادِهِ بِصِدْقٍ وَاحِدٍ. قَالَ فِي «الْحَاشِيَةِ»: ذَكَرَهُ الْمُحَقِّقُ الدَّوَانِي فِي «الْحَاشِيَةِ الْقَدِيمَةِ»، فَمَجْمُوعُ الْإِنْسَانِ وَالْفَرَسِ حَيَوَانٌ، فَلَهُ فَصْلَانِ قَرِيبَانِ: النَّاطِقُ وَالصَّاهِلُ. لَا يُقَالُ: الْمُقَدِّمَةُ الْمُمَهِّدَةُ بَاطِلَةٌ؛ إِذْ يَلْزَمُ صِدْقُ الْعِلَّةِ عَلَى ...
The second: what occurred to me, which is that the universal just as it applies to one of its individuals applies to many of its individuals with one application. He said in the Hashiya: al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawani mentioned it in the old Hashiya. So the sum of human and horse is animal, so it has two proximate differentiae: rational and neighing. It cannot be said: the established premise is false; because it would necessitate that the cause applies to ...
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage presents the second aspect of the famous doubt. The author introduces a personal observation: a universal (kulli) applies to many individuals with a single application. For example, the universal 'animal' applies to both human and horse. This implies that the aggregate of human and horse is animal, so the genus 'animal' would have two proximate differentiae: rational (for human) and neighing (for horse). The objection that the premise is false begins but the text is incomplete. The reader is left to infer that the objection might be that the same universal cannot have two differentiae.

Key Takeaway
The doubt shows that if a universal applies uniformly to multiple species, the aggregate of those species would have multiple differentiae, challenging the classical principle of one differentia per species.

The Universal Applies to Many with One Application
Author defines the universal and defends its application against an objection about composite causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the property of the universal as applying to many individuals with one application and defend it against the objection from composite causes using the distinction of aspects.

Core Idea
The universal applies to many individuals with a single predication, not multiple separate ones.

In this passage, the author defines the universal (al-kulli) and clarifies a crucial property: it is true of many individuals with one application. He then addresses an objection that would seem to undermine this property, involving composite causes. By distinguishing between aspects of unity and multiplicity, he shows that no contradiction arises.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of the universal
Find the phrase that defines al-kulli. The text says: 'al-kulliyu... yasduqu 'ala kathirina min afradihi bi-sidqin wahid' – the universal is true of many of its individuals with one truth.
2
Examine the example from al-Dawani
Al-Dawani gives: 'the sum of man and horse is animal, so it has two proximate differentiae' (rational and neighing). This shows that the universal 'animal' applies to both species with a single concept.
3
Analyze the objection
The objection claims that if the universal applies to a composite effect, then truth of cause upon the composite effect would be impossible because each part (matter and form) is a cause.
4
Understand the refutation
The author denies the impossibility: the composite has two aspects – as an effect it is one, as a cause it is multiple. So it is both one effect and multiple causes without contradiction.
The key is the distinction of considerations (i'tibar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالثَّاني: مَا سَنَحَ لي، وَهُوَ أَنَّ الْكُلِّيَّ كَمَا يَصْدُقُ عَلَى وَاحِدٍ مِنْ أَفْرَادِهِ يَصْدُقُ عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ مِنْ أَفْرَادِهِ بِصِدْقٍ وَاحِدٍ). قال في «الحاشية»: ذكره المحقق الدواني في «الحاشية القديمة»، (فَمَجْمُوعُ الْإِنْسَانِ وَالْفَرَسِ حَيَوَانٌ، فَلَهُ فَصْلَانِ قَرِيبَانِ)، وهما الناطق والصاهل. (لَا يُقَالُ): المقدمة الممهدة باطلة؛ إذ (يَلْزَمُ صِدْقُ الْعِلَّةِ عَلَى الْمَعْلُولِ الْمُرَكَّب؛ لِأَنَّهُ مَجْمُوعُ الْمَادِّيَّةِ وَالصُّورِيَّةِ، ويصدق على كل منهما أنه علة، فيلزم الصدق على مجموعهما، وَهُوَ مُحَالٌ؛ [وَذَلِكَ] لِأَنَّ الاسْتِحَالَةَ، أي استحالة صدق العلة على المجموع (مَمْنُوعَةٌ، فَإِنَّهُ) [لَهُ] جِهَتَانِ جِهَةُ الْوَحْدَةِ، وَبِهَذِهِ الْجِهَةِ مَعْلُولٌ، فَهُوَ مَعْلُولٌ وَاحِدٌ، وَجِهَةُ الْكَثْرَةِ، وَبِهَا عِلَّةٌ، فَهُوَ عِلَّةٌ كَثِيرَةٌ، فَاخْتَلَفَا اعْتِبَارًا.
And the second: what occurred to me, and it is that the universal, just as it is true of one of its individuals, is true of many of its individuals with one truth. He said in al-Hashiya: al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawani mentioned it in al-Hashiya al-Qadima: 'The sum of man and horse is animal, so it has two proximate differentiae,' namely rational and neighing. It is not said: The preparatory premise is false; for it would necessitate the truth of the cause upon the composite effect, because it is the sum of matter and form, and each of them is said to be a cause, so truth upon their sum would follow, and that is impossible. And that is because the impossibility, i.e., the impossibility of the truth of the cause upon the sum, is denied. For it has two aspects: an aspect of unity, and in that aspect it is an effect, so it is a single effect; and an aspect of multiplicity, and in that aspect it is a cause, so it is a multiple cause. So they differ in consideration.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on a definition of the universal (al-kulli). The author presents a second point: the universal applies to many individuals with a single application (bi-sidqin wahid). He cites al-Dawani's Hashiyah, which gives an example: the sum of 'man' and 'horse' is 'animal'; therefore 'animal' has two proximate differentiae (rational and neighing), each specific to a species. This illustrates that a universal can be predicated of multiple individuals with one meaning. An objection is then raised: if a universal applies to a composite, then truth of the cause upon the composite effect would be impossible. But the author refutes this by distinguishing aspects: the composite has an aspect of unity (as an effect) and an aspect of multiplicity (as a cause). As an effect, it is one; as a cause, it is multiple. Thus no impossibility arises—they differ in consideration (i'tibar).

الصدق
العلة

D) It applies only to composites.

Key Takeaway
The universal applies to many individuals with a single application; apparent contradictions are resolved by considering different aspects.

The Universal Does Not Apply to a Composite as a Unit
Author refutes universal applying to composite of instances

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute the claim that a universal predicate applies to a composite of its individuals as a single entity, and to distinguish between essential and accidental predication in definitions.

Core Idea
A universal applies to each instance separately, not to the set as a whole.

This passage addresses a subtle confusion: if the universal 'animal' applies to 'human' and 'horse' individually, does it also apply to the composite 'human and horse' as one animal? The author shows this is not the case, because the composite is not an essential subject of the universal and would require impossible differentiae. This clarification is crucial for understanding how definitions work: a definition's genus and differentia apply to the species, not to aggregates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
The claim is that a universal applies to a multitude of its individuals as it does to a single individual. Find this claim in the Arabic: 'الكلي كما يصدق على واحد كذلك على الكثير'.
2
Examine the first rejection: individuals are external parts
The author says the individuals are external parts of the composite, so what is true of them is not necessarily true of the composite. For example, 'animal' is true of human and horse individually, but not of the composite human+horse as one animal.
3
Analyze the differentia problem
If the composite were a single animal, it would need a single differentia. But each part has its own differentia (rational for human, whinnying for horse), and one thing cannot have two differentiae. This is a key argument.
4
Understand the correct meaning of applying to many
The universal applies to many individuals individually, not as a collective. The author says 'but by many applications' (بأصداق كثيرة), not a single application to the set.
5
Consider the infinite regress objection and its solution
The objection: if from two you get a third composite, then from three a fourth, ad infinitum. The solution: the fourth (and subsequent) are merely conceptual (اعتباري), not real; they result from considering the same thing twice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَحَلُّهُ: أَنَّ وُجُودَ اثْنَيْنِ يَسْتَلْزِمُ وُجُودَ ثَالِثٍ، وَهُوَ الْمَجْمُوعُ، وَذَلِكَ وَاحِدٌ. قال في «الحاشية»: وذلك لأن لكل افتقارا دون الأجزاء، ولو كان للأجزاء افتقار فهناك إمكان دون إمكان الأجزاء، فهناك وجود دون وجود الأجزاء. اعلم أن الحق في الحل أن يقال: إن أريد بقوله «الكلي كما يصدق على واحد كذلك على الكثير أنه يصدق على مجموع كثير مركب من أفراده معروض للهيئة داخلة أو عارضة له ، فلا نسلم ذلك، كيف والأفراد من أجزائه الخارجية، ولا يلزم صدق ما يصدق عليها عليه ، ولو سلم فلا نسلم صدقه صدقا ذاتيا ، فلا نسلم أن مجموع الإنسان والفرس حيوان، أو لو سلم فلا نسلم كونه ذاتيا وجنسا، فلا يحتاج إلى فصل، ولو سلم فلا نسلم كون كل واحد من الناطق والصاهل فصلا له ؛ لامتناع الحمل، ولزوم كون شيء واحد فصلا لنوعين المركب وأحد أجزائه ، بل الفصل إنما يؤخذ من جزئه الصوري لو كان . وإن أريد أنه يصدق على الكثير من حيث إنه كثير فالصدق مسلم، لكن لا بصدق واحد، بل بأصداق كثيرة ، فليس مجموع الفرس والإنسان حيوانا واحدا، فلا يحتاج إلى الفصل، هذا والله أعلم بالصواب. فتأمل فيه ؛ فإنه يظهر منه عدم تمامية الحل المذكور في المتن . لَا يُقَالُ: عَلَى هَذَا يَلْزَمُ مِنْ تَحَقُّقِ اثْنَيْنِ تَحَقُّقُ أُمُورٍ غَيْر مُتَنَاهِيَةِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ بِضَمِّ الثَّالِثِ يَتَحَقَّقُ الرَّابِعُ وَهَكَذَا ، يتحقق الخامس؛ لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ: الرَّابِعُ أَمْرٌ اعْتِبَارِيُّ ، فَإِنَّهُ حَصَلَ بِاعْتِبَارِ شَيْءٍ وَاحِدٍ، وهو كل واحد من الاثنين مَرَّتَيْنِ: مرة بنفسه، ومرة في ضمن المجموع، وكل ما هو كذلك فهو اعتباري؛ إذ لو كان موجودا في الأعيان كان جزء المتكرر مقدما عليه مرة بمرتبة لكونه جزء له ومرة بمرتبتين لكونه جزء جزء، فيلزم أن يكون موجودا
And its solution: that the existence of two entails the existence of a third, which is the composite, and that is one. He said in al-Hashiyah: That is because each has a need apart from the parts; and if the parts had a need, then there is a possibility apart from the possibility of the parts, so there is an existence apart from the existence of the parts. Know that the truth in the solution is that it is said: If by his statement 'the universal as it applies to one, likewise to many' is meant that it applies to a composite multitude composed of its individuals presented to an internal or accidental form, then we do not accept that; how so, while the individuals are from its external parts, and what applies to them does not necessarily apply to it. And even if accepted, we do not accept that its applicability is essential, so we do not accept that the composite of human and horse is an animal; or if accepted, we do not accept it as essential and a genus, so it does not need a differentia; and if accepted, we do not accept that each of 'rational' and 'whinnying' is a differentia for it, because of the impossibility of predication and the necessity of one thing being a differentia for two species (the composite and one of its parts). Rather, the differentia is taken from its formal part, if it has one. And if it is meant that it applies to the many insofar as they are many, then the applicability is granted, but not by a single application, but by many applications; so the composite of horse and human is not one animal, so it does not need a differentia. This, and God knows best the truth. So reflect on it; for it shows the incompleteness of the solution mentioned in the matn. It is not said: upon this, from the realization of two, the realization of infinite things would follow, because by adding the third, the fourth is realized, and so on, the fifth is realized; because we say: the fourth is a conceptual matter, for it occurs by considering one thing (each of the two) twice: once by itself, and once within the composite; and everything that is like that is conceptual; for if it existed in reals, the repeated part would be prior to it once by one rank because it is a part of it, and once by two ranks because it is a part of a part, so it would have to exist...
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on a solution (الحل) proposed in the matn regarding the universal and the composite. The author begins by stating the solution: the existence of two things entails the existence of a third, which is the composite of the two, and that composite is one thing. A gloss (al-Hashiyah) clarifies that each has a need independent of the parts. Then the author provides the true analysis: if by 'the universal applies to many as it does to one' it is meant that the universal applies to a composite set of its individuals, then this is rejected. Why? Because the individuals are external parts of the composite, and what is true of them is not necessarily true of the composite. Even if one concedes that the composite is described by the universal, it would not be as an essential attribute; for example, the composite of 'human' and 'horse' is not an animal in the sense of a single animal. Consequently, it does not require a differentia. If one insists, then each differentia (rational for human, whinnying for horse) cannot both be differentiae for the composite, as they would be predicated of different parts. The correct view is that if the universal is said to apply to many qua many, then it applies with multiple applications (each individual is an animal), not a single application to the set. The author then introduces a further objection: this solution would lead to an infinite regress because combining two into one yields a third, and then adding the third yields a fourth, ad infinitum. The response is that the fourth is a conceptual (اعتباري) entity, not real; it results from considering the same thing twice (once by itself and once in the composite). If it were real, it would force an absurdity of a part being prior in two different ranks. The passage concludes with an invitation to reflect, implying the solution in the matn is incomplete.

مركب
فصل
اعتباري
جزء صوري

The Composite Universal: Why Man and Horse Cannot Form a Single Genus
Resolves objection about composite universals and infinite regress

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why a composite of different species cannot be a single universal genus and explain the dialectical steps in rejecting that claim.

Core Idea
A composite of different species cannot be a single essential universal because it lacks a unitive differentia.

In this passage, the commentator engages a dialectical objection: can a composite of individuals like man and horse be a single universal (e.g., animal)? He systematically rejects this, showing that such a composite fails to be a true genus and cannot have a proper differentia.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Opponent's Claim
The opponent asserts that a composite (majmūʿ) of many individuals can be a single universal predicated of many.
2
First Rejection: External Parts
The commentator denies the claim because the individuals are external parts of the composite, so predication of the whole to the parts does not hold.
3
Second Rejection: Essential Truth
Even if true, the predication is not essential (dhātī), so the composite cannot be a genus.
4
Third Rejection: Differentia Problem
If it were a genus, it would need a differentia, but neither 'rational' nor 'neighing' can serve as a differentia for both the composite and its parts.
5
Alternative Explanation
If the composite is predicated of many qua many, it is not a single truth but many truths, so no differentia is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الكليات الخمس واحد كذلك على الكثير أنه يصدق على مجموع كثير مركب من أفراده معروض للهيئة داخلة أو عارضة له ، فلا نسلم ذلك، كيف والأفراد من أجزائه الخارجية، ولا يلزم صدق ما يصدق عليها عليه ، ولو سلم فلا نسلم صدقه صدقا ذاتيا ، فلا نسلم أن مجموع الإنسان والفرس حيوان، أو لو سلم فلا نسلم كونه ذاتيا وجنسا، فلا يحتاج إلى فصل، ولو سلم فلا نسلم كون كل واحد من الناطق والصاهل فصلا له ؛ لامتناع الحمل، ولزوم كون شيء واحد فصلا لنوعين المركب وأحد أجزائه ، بل الفصل إنما يؤخذ من جزئه الصوري لو كان . وإن أريد أنه يصدق على الكثير من حيث إنه كثير فالصدق مسلم، لكن لا بصدق واحد، بل بأصداق كثيرة ، فليس مجموع الفرس والإنسان حيوانا واحدا، فلا يحتاج إلى الفصل، هذا والله أعلم بالصواب. فتأمل فيه ؛ فإنه يظهر منه عدم تمامية الحل المذكور في المتن . (1) لَا يُقَالُ: عَلَى هَذَا يَلْزَمُ مِنْ تَحَقُّقِ اثْنَيْنِ تَحَقُّقُ أُمُورٍ غَيْر مُتَنَاهِيَةِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ بِضَمِّ الثَّالِثِ يَتَحَقَّقُ الرَّابِعُ وَهَكَذَا (۲) ، يتحقق الخامس؛ لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ: الرَّابِعُ أَمْرُ (۳) اعْتِبَارِيُّ ، فَإِنَّهُ حَصَلَ بِاعْتِبَارِ شَيْءٍ وَاحِدٍ)، وهو كل واحد من الاثنين ( مَرَّتَيْنِ): مرة بنفسه، ومرة في ضمن المجموع، وكل ما هو كذلك فهو اعتباري؛ إذ لو كان موجودا في الأعيان كان جزء المتكرر مقدما عليه مرة بمرتبة لكونه جزء له ومرة بمرتبتين لكونه جزء جزء، فيلزم أن يكون موجودا بوجودين ، وهو محال . شرح بحر العلوم على سلم العلوم فإن قلت : الهيولى جزء مكرر لجسم مركب ؟ قلت: هو مكرر بوحدتها المبهمة، والله أعلم بالصواب. وإذا تمهد هذا فنقول تلك الأمور اعتباريات، (وَالتَسَلْسُلُ الاعْتِبَارِيَّاتُ مُنْقَطِعٌ بِانْقِطَاعِهِ) (۱) ، أي بانقطاع الاعتبار، فلم يلزم تحقق أمور غير متناهية، (فَافْهَمْ)، وكن على بصيرة وتوكل على الله تعالى؛ فإنه أعلم بالصواب.
Chapter on the five universals. Similarly, that it is predicated of many that it is true of a composite multitude composed of its individuals, presented to an internal or accidental form. We do not accept that. How so? The individuals are among its external parts. And it does not necessitate that what is true of them is true of it. Even if accepted, we do not accept that its truth is essential truth. So we do not accept that the composite of man and horse is an animal. Or if accepted, we do not accept that it is essential and a genus, so it does not need a differentia. And if accepted, we do not accept that each of 'rational' and 'neighing' is a differentia for it, because of the impossibility of predication and the necessity that one thing be a differentia for two species: the composite and one of its parts. Rather, the differentia is taken from its formal part if it had one. And if it is meant that it is predicated of many insofar as it is many, then the truth is accepted, but not with one truth, but with many truths. So the composite of horse and man is not one animal, so it does not need a differentia. This, and Allah knows best what is correct. So reflect on it; for it shows the incompleteness of the solution mentioned in the text. (1) It cannot be said: According to this, from the existence of two things, the existence of infinite things would follow, because by combining the third, the fourth exists, and so on, the fifth exists. Because we say: The fourth is a conceptual matter, for it is obtained by considering one thing twice: once by itself, and once as part of the composite. And everything like that is conceptual; for if it existed in external entities, then the repeated part would be prior to it once by one rank because it is a part of it, and once by two ranks because it is a part of a part, so it would exist with two existences, which is impossible. Commentary of Bahr Ulum on Sullum Ulum. If you say: Hyle is a repeated part of a composite body? I say: It is repeated by its vague unity, and Allah knows best. And when this is established, we say: Those matters are conceptual, and the chain of conceptual things is broken by its cessation, i.e., by the cessation of consideration, so the existence of infinite things does not follow. So understand, and be insightful, and rely on Allah Almighty; for He knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This is a dialectical passage where the commentator addresses an objection regarding the concept of the composite universal and the problem of infinite regress. The discussion begins with a rejection of the claim that a composite of individuals (like 'man and horse') can be a single universal (like 'animal') that is predicated essentially. The commentator argues that such a composite is not one thing but many, and that if it were a universal, it would require a differentia, which is impossible. The objection then raises a concern: if combining two things necessarily produces a third, fourth, etc., this leads to an infinite regress of actual entities. The response is that the resulting 'fourth' (the composite of two and the third) is merely a conceptual (i'tibari) being, not an external one, because it arises from considering the same thing twice (once alone, once as part of the composite). If it were external, the repeated part would have to exist with multiple existences simultaneously, which is impossible. An additional question about hyle (matter) in a composite body is answered similarly: hyle is repeated by its vague unity, not as a real multiplicity. Therefore, the chain of conceptual entities is broken when the act of consideration stops, so no actual infinite regress follows. The passage ends with an exhortation to understand and rely on Allah.

تسلسل

Infinite Regress of Conceptual Entities: How Consideration Stops the Chain
Resolves objection about composite universals and infinite regress

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between actual and conceptual infinite regress and apply the reasoning to show that a regress of conceptual entities does not entail an actual infinite chain.

Core Idea
An infinite regress of conceptual entities is broken when the act of consideration stops; it does not produce actual infinite things.

An objection is raised: if from two things a third always follows, then an infinite regress of actual entities would result. The commentator responds by clarifying that the resulting entities are merely conceptual (i'tibari), not external. He provides a criterion: if something arises from considering one thing twice, it is conceptual. This resolves the apparent infinite regress.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Objection
The opponent argues that from the existence of two things, combining them with a third yields a fourth, then a fifth, ad infinitum, leading to an infinite number of actual things.
2
Identify the Response: Conceptual Status
The commentator says the fourth (the composite) is conceptual (i'tibari), because it results from considering one thing twice: once by itself, once as part of the composite.
3
Apply the Criterion
Anything that arises from considering the same thing in multiple ways without external multiplicity is conceptual. If it were external, the repeated part would have to exist with multiple existences simultaneously, which is impossible.
4
Address the Hyle Question
The commentator answers an objection about hyle (prime matter) being a repeated part of a composite body: hyle is repeated by its vague unity, not as a real multiplicity.
5
Conclude: No Actual Infinity
Since the entities are conceptual, the chain stops when the consideration stops. No actual infinite regress follows.

فصل في الكليات الخمس واحد كذلك على الكثير أنه يصدق على مجموع كثير مركب من أفراده معروض للهيئة داخلة أو عارضة له ، فلا نسلم ذلك، كيف والأفراد من أجزائه الخارجية، ولا يلزم صدق ما يصدق عليها عليه ، ولو سلم فلا نسلم صدقه صدقا ذاتيا ، فلا نسلم أن مجموع الإنسان والفرس حيوان، أو لو سلم فلا نسلم كونه ذاتيا وجنسا، فلا يحتاج إلى فصل، ولو سلم فلا نسلم كون كل واحد من الناطق والصاهل فصلا له ؛ لامتناع الحمل، ولزوم كون شيء واحد فصلا لنوعين المركب وأحد أجزائه ، بل الفصل إنما يؤخذ من جزئه الصوري لو كان . وإن أريد أنه يصدق على الكثير من حيث إنه كثير فالصدق مسلم، لكن لا بصدق واحد، بل بأصداق كثيرة ، فليس مجموع الفرس والإنسان حيوانا واحدا، فلا يحتاج إلى الفصل، هذا والله أعلم بالصواب. فتأمل فيه ؛ فإنه يظهر منه عدم تمامية الحل المذكور في المتن . (1) لَا يُقَالُ: عَلَى هَذَا يَلْزَمُ مِنْ تَحَقُّقِ اثْنَيْنِ تَحَقُّقُ أُمُورٍ غَيْر مُتَنَاهِيَةِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ بِضَمِّ الثَّالِثِ يَتَحَقَّقُ الرَّابِعُ وَهَكَذَا (۲) ، يتحقق الخامس؛ لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ: الرَّابِعُ أَمْرُ (۳) اعْتِبَارِيُّ ، فَإِنَّهُ حَصَلَ بِاعْتِبَارِ شَيْءٍ وَاحِدٍ)، وهو كل واحد من الاثنين ( مَرَّتَيْنِ): مرة بنفسه، ومرة في ضمن المجموع، وكل ما هو كذلك فهو اعتباري؛ إذ لو كان موجودا في الأعيان كان جزء المتكرر مقدما عليه مرة بمرتبة لكونه جزء له ومرة بمرتبتين لكونه جزء جزء، فيلزم أن يكون موجودا بوجودين ، وهو محال . شرح بحر العلوم على سلم العلوم فإن قلت : الهيولى جزء مكرر لجسم مركب ؟ قلت: هو مكرر بوحدتها المبهمة، والله أعلم بالصواب. وإذا تمهد هذا فنقول تلك الأمور اعتباريات، (وَالتَسَلْسُلُ الاعْتِبَارِيَّاتُ مُنْقَطِعٌ بِانْقِطَاعِهِ) (۱) ، أي بانقطاع الاعتبار، فلم يلزم تحقق أمور غير متناهية، (فَافْهَمْ)، وكن على بصيرة وتوكل على الله تعالى؛ فإنه أعلم بالصواب.
Chapter on the five universals. Similarly, that it is predicated of many that it is true of a composite multitude composed of its individuals, presented to an internal or accidental form. We do not accept that. How so? The individuals are among its external parts. And it does not necessitate that what is true of them is true of it. Even if accepted, we do not accept that its truth is essential truth. So we do not accept that the composite of man and horse is an animal. Or if accepted, we do not accept that it is essential and a genus, so it does not need a differentia. And if accepted, we do not accept that each of 'rational' and 'neighing' is a differentia for it, because of the impossibility of predication and the necessity that one thing be a differentia for two species: the composite and one of its parts. Rather, the differentia is taken from its formal part if it had one. And if it is meant that it is predicated of many insofar as it is many, then the truth is accepted, but not with one truth, but with many truths. So the composite of horse and man is not one animal, so it does not need a differentia. This, and Allah knows best what is correct. So reflect on it; for it shows the incompleteness of the solution mentioned in the text. (1) It cannot be said: According to this, from the existence of two things, the existence of infinite things would follow, because by combining the third, the fourth exists, and so on, the fifth exists. Because we say: The fourth is a conceptual matter, for it is obtained by considering one thing twice: once by itself, and once as part of the composite. And everything like that is conceptual; for if it existed in external entities, then the repeated part would be prior to it once by one rank because it is a part of it, and once by two ranks because it is a part of a part, so it would exist with two existences, which is impossible. Commentary of Bahr Ulum on Sullum Ulum. If you say: Hyle is a repeated part of a composite body? I say: It is repeated by its vague unity, and Allah knows best. And when this is established, we say: Those matters are conceptual, and the chain of conceptual things is broken by its cessation, i.e., by the cessation of consideration, so the existence of infinite things does not follow. So understand, and be insightful, and rely on Allah Almighty; for He knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This is a dialectical passage where the commentator addresses an objection regarding the concept of the composite universal and the problem of infinite regress. The discussion begins with a rejection of the claim that a composite of individuals (like 'man and horse') can be a single universal (like 'animal') that is predicated essentially. The commentator argues that such a composite is not one thing but many, and that if it were a universal, it would require a differentia, which is impossible. The objection then raises a concern: if combining two things necessarily produces a third, fourth, etc., this leads to an infinite regress of actual entities. The response is that the resulting 'fourth' (the composite of two and the third) is merely a conceptual (i'tibari) being, not an external one, because it arises from considering the same thing twice (once alone, once as part of the composite). If it were external, the repeated part would have to exist with multiple existences simultaneously, which is impossible. An additional question about hyle (matter) in a composite body is answered similarly: hyle is repeated by its vague unity, not as a real multiplicity. Therefore, the chain of conceptual entities is broken when the act of consideration stops, so no actual infinite regress follows. The passage ends with an exhortation to understand and rely on Allah.

اعتباري
تسلسل
هيولى

Checkpoint

A) Because the composites are external
B) Because the regress is conceptual, not actual
C) Because the number of entities is finite
D) Because the third thing does not exist

Key Takeaway
An infinite regress of conceptual entities does not entail an actual infinite regress because conceptual existence depends on mental consideration.

The Five Universals

The Fourth Universal: Al-Khassah (Property)
Defines the fourth universal al-khassah and its types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the essential property (al-haqiqiyyah) from the relational property (al-idafiyyah) and identify whether a given property is comprehensive or non-comprehensive.

Core Idea
A property (khassah) is a predicate external to the essence, but it has layers: essential vs relational, comprehensive vs non-comprehensive.

The fourth of the five universals is al-khassah, the property or accident. Unlike the first three universals (genus, species, differentia), the property is not part of the essence—it is a predicate that applies to individuals sharing a single essence, but from outside that essence. In this passage, the author clarifies that there are two main types: essential properties that are exclusive to that essence, and relational properties that may also apply to other essences. Understanding this distinction is crucial for evaluating definitions in Islamic sciences, such as when jurists define 'riba' or mutakallimun define 'qadim'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Locate the term being defined: al-khassah (the property). Notice that the definition begins by stating it is a universal that is external to the essence of its individuals.
2
Distinguish the two main types based on scope
The passage distinguishes essential (haqiqiyyah) and relational (idafiyyah) properties. Essential property applies only to individuals under one essence (e.g., 'writer' for man). Relational property may apply to other essences (e.g., 'walker' for man and horse).
The essential property is called 'haqiqiyyah' because it is true of that essence alone.
3
Understand comprehensive vs non-comprehensive
Within the essential property, it can be comprehensive (shamilah) if it applies to all individuals of that essence (e.g., 'potential writer' for all humans) or non-comprehensive (ghayr shamilah) if only some (e.g., 'actual writer' for those who write).
Comprehensiveness depends on whether the property holds for every individual of the essence.
4
Assess the misconception
The passage warns against thinking that a non-comprehensive property is essentially predicated of the more specific and accidentally of the more general. It rejects this view, citing Avicenna's statement that the differentia is an essential accident of the genus.
This shows how careful one must be when analyzing property predication across levels of generality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْمَبْحَثُ الرَّابِعُ: الْخَاصَّةُ. الكلي الرَّابِعُ: الْخَاصَّةُ، هُوَ: الكلي الْخَارج عن حقيقة أفراده، الْمَقُولُ عَلَى مَا تَحْتَ حَقِيقَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ، نَوْعِيَّةٍ، كالكاتب، أَوْ جِنْسِيَّةٍ، كالماشي، وقد يخص باسم الحقيقة، وقد يقال لما يحمل على ما تحت حقيقة، ولا يحمل على واحدة أخرى، ويسمى إضافية، وهي أعم من الحقيقية، كالماشي خاصة للإنسان بالنسبة إلى الشيء، وَهِيَ شَامِلَةٌ إِنْ عَمَّتِ الْأَفْرَادَ كلَّها، كالكاتب بالقوة للإنسان، وَإِلَّا يَعُمَّ فَغَيْرُ شَامِلَةٍ، كالكاتب بالفعل له. وربما يظن أن غير الشاملة خاصة للأخص حقيقة، والأعم بالعرض، وهذا لا يتم إلا إذا كان الأخص واسطة في عروضها للأعم، وهو ممنوع، كيف وقد قال الشيخ في «الشفاء»: الفصل عرض ذاتي للجنس، والله أعلم.
The fourth topic: The property. The fourth universal: the property, it is: the universal that is external to the essence of its individuals, predicated of what is under one essence, either a species-essence, like 'writer', or a genus-essence, like 'walker'. And it may be specified by the name 'essential', and it may be said of that which is predicated of what is under an essence but is not predicated of any other, and it is called 'relational', and it is more general than the essential, like 'walker' is a property for man relative to a thing. And it is comprehensive if it encompasses all individuals, like 'writer in potentiality' for man; otherwise, if not comprehensive, it is non-comprehensive, like 'writer in actuality' for him. And sometimes it is thought that the non-comprehensive is a property for the more specific essentially, and the more general accidentally. But this is not complete unless the more specific is an intermediary in its occurrence to the more general, which is denied. How so? For the Shaykh said in al-Shifa: The differentia is an essential accident of the genus. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth of the five universals: al-khassah (the property/accident). It is a universal that is not part of the essence of its individuals (i.e., not a constitutive part) but is predicated of them. It can be predicated of individuals that share a single essence, either a species-essence (like 'writer' for man) or a genus-essence (like 'walker' for both man and horse). The property is sometimes called 'essential' (al-haqiqiyyah) when it is coextensive with the essence, or 'relational' (al-idafiyyah) when it is broader. For example, 'walker' is a property for man relative to a thing (like an animal) because it applies to more than just man. The property can be comprehensive (shamilah) if it applies to all individuals of that essence, like 'potential writer' for all men, or non-comprehensive (ghayr shamilah) if it applies only to some, like 'actual writer' for only those who write. A common misconception is that the non-comprehensive property is essentially a property of the more specific (e.g., 'actual writer' is essential for the man who writes) and accidentally of the more general (man). But the author rejects this, citing Avicenna's statement that the differentia (like rational) is an essential accident of the genus (animal), meaning it is not essentially predicated of the genus. The same applies here: the non-comprehensive property is not essentially a property of the more general.

Key Terms
خاصة
حقيقية
إضافية
شاملة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Essential property is predicated of one species only; relational property is predicated of multiple species
B) Essential property is part of the essence; relational property is external to the essence
C) Essential property is not predicated of anything outside the essence; relational property may be predicated of other essences
D) Essential property is comprehensive; relational property is non-comprehensive

Key Takeaway
The property (khassah) is defined as a universal external to the essence, and it is subdivided into essential (exclusive) and relational (broader), as well as comprehensive (covering all individuals) and non-comprehensive (covering only some).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the property 'requires ablution' for the species 'minor ritual impurity' (hadath asghar). Is it an essential property (haqiqiyyah) or relational (idafiyyah)? Explain why.
?

Understanding al-Khassa (Proprium) and Its Types
Author defines al-khassa, distinguishes shamila and ghayr shamila, and refutes a misconception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the proprium among the five universals and distinguish comprehensive from non-comprehensive propria in Islamic logical definitions.

Core Idea
A proprium tells you what necessarily accompanies a species, not what makes it what it is.

This passage introduces the fourth universal, al-khassa (proprium). Unlike the differentia (fasl) which is part of the essence, a proprium is an attribute that necessarily belongs to all members of a species or genus but is not part of the definition. The author also distinguishes between comprehensive and non-comprehensive propria and warns against a common misunderstanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining characteristic
Note that a proprium is external to the essence (haqiqa) of individuals. It is predicated on all members of a single reality (species or genus).
2
Distinguish real vs relative proprium
Real proprium is exclusive to that reality; relative proprium is more general but still predicated.
Example: 'walker' is relative for man because it applies to other animals too.
3
Differentiate comprehensive vs non-comprehensive
Comprehensive applies to all individuals (e.g., potential writer for all humans), non-comprehensive only to some (e.g., actual writer for some humans).
4
Refute the misconception
The author rejects the idea that non-comprehensive proprium is real for the more specific and accidental for the more general, citing Ibn Sina's statement that the differentia is an accidental property of the genus.
This prevents confusion about the logical status of non-comprehensive propria.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْمَبْحَثُ الرَّابِعُ: الْخَاصَّةُ . الكلي الرَّابِعُ: الْخَاصَّةُ ، هو: الكلي الْخَارج عن حقيقة أفراده، الْمَقُولُ عَلَى مَا تَحْتَ حَقِيقَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ، نَوْعِيَّةٍ، كالكاتب، أَوْ جِنْسِيَّةٍ، كالماشي، وقد يخص باسم الحقيقة، وقد يقال لما يحمل على ما تحت حقيقة، ولا يحمل على واحدة أخرى، ويسمى إضافية، وهي أعم من الحقيقية، كالماشي خاصة للإنسان بالنسبة إلى الشيء، وَهِيَ شَامِلَةٌ إِنْ عَمَّتِ الْأَفْرَادَ كلَّها ، كالكاتب بالقوة للإنسان، وَإِلَّا يَعُمَّ فَغَيْرُ شَامِلَةٍ، كالكاتب بالفعل له. وربما يظن أن غير الشاملة خاصة للأخص حقيقة، والأعم بالعرض، وهذا لا يتم إلا إذا كان الأخص واسطة في عروضها للأعم، وهو ممنوع ، كيف وقد قال الشيخ في «الشفاء»: الفصل عرض ذاتي للجنس، والله أعلم .
The fourth investigation: Proprium. The fourth universal: Proprium, it is: the universal external to the reality of its individuals, predicated on what is under a single reality, whether specific, like 'writer', or generic, like 'walker'. And it may be specialized by the name of reality, and it may be said for what is predicated on what is under a reality, and is not predicated on any other, and it is called relative, and it is more general than the real, like 'walker' is a proprium for man relative to a thing. And it is comprehensive if it includes all individuals, like 'writer in potentiality' for man, and if not, it is non-comprehensive, like 'writer in actuality' for him. And perhaps one thinks that the non-comprehensive is a proprium for the more specific in reality, and the more general accidentally, but this is not valid unless the more specific is a medium in its occurrence to the more general, and this is denied, especially since the Sheikh said in al-Shifa': The differentia is an accidental property of the genus. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth universal, al-khassa (proprium). A proprium is a universal that is external to the essence of its individuals—meaning it is not part of the definition—but is predicated on all members of a single reality (either a species or a genus). Examples: 'writer' for a species, 'walker' for a genus. It can be called 'real' proprium if it is exclusive to that reality, or 'relative' if it is more general (like 'walker' for man relative to a thing). Then the passage divides proprium into comprehensive (shamila) and non-comprehensive (ghayr shamila). Comprehensive covers all individuals of that reality (e.g., potential writer), non-comprehensive covers only some (e.g., actual writer). A common mistake is thinking that non-comprehensive proprium is real for the more specific and accidental for the more general, but the author refutes this, citing Ibn Sina's al-Shifa' that the differentia (fasl) is an accidental property of the genus, implying that the relation is not as assumed.

Key Terms
خاصة
شاملة
غير شاملة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a non-comprehensive (ghayr shamila) proprium according to the passage?
A) 'Rational' for all humans
B) 'Writer in potentiality' for all humans
C) 'Writer in actuality' for some humans
D) 'Walker' for the genus of animals

Key Takeaway
A proprium is a non-essential universal that always accompanies a species, but it may be comprehensive (applying to all individuals) or non-comprehensive (applying only to some).

Definition and Division of the General Accident (al-'Arad al-'Amm)
Author defines al-'arad al-'amm, divides it into necessary/separable, and further subdivides necessary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-'arad al-'amm and classify accidents as necessary or separable, including the subtypes of necessary accidents.

Core Idea
The general accident is an external universal predicated on diverse essences; its necessary type is impossible to separate.

This passage introduces the fifth universal, al-'arad al-'amm. You will learn its precise definition and the important division into necessary (lazim) and separable (mufariq) accidents. Understanding this classification is crucial for correctly applying definitions and descriptions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term being defined: al-'arad al-'amm (general accident). The author gives its definition as 'the universal external to the essence predicated on diverse realities'.
2
Extract the genus and differentia
The genus is 'universal' (kulli) and the differentia is 'external to the essence and predicated on diverse realities'. This distinguishes it from essential predicates and the proprium.
3
Differentiate from the proprium
Note that both are accidents, but the proprium (خَاصَّة) is predicated on only one essence, while the general accident applies to multiple distinct essences.
Example: 'walker' can be said of both man and horse, so it is a general accident.
4
Analyse the division into necessary and separable
The author divides accidents into necessary (if separation is impossible) and separable (if separation is possible). Separable accidents are further divided by duration: quick (redness of shyness), slow (infatuation), or permanent (celestial motion).
The passage notes that this division is preliminary; philosophy holds that even permanent accidents are not truly separable without a cause.
5
Examine the subdivision of necessary accidents
Necessary accidents are subdivided into: (1) lazim al-mahiyya (necessary of the essence) – impossible to separate from the essence in any existence, e.g., contingency; (2) secondary intelligible (ma'qul thani) – impossible to separate in mental existence only, e.g., categoricalness.
The passage also notes that perpetuity requires causal necessity, so even necessary accidents depend on causes.

فصل في الكليات الخمس الْمَبْحَثُ الْخَامِسُ الْعَرَضُ الْعَامُ ) الكلي الْخَامِسُ : الْعَرَضُ الْعَامُّ ، وَهُوَ الكلي الْخَارِجُ الْمَقُولُ عَلَى حَقَائِقَ مُخْتَلِفَةٍ، كالماشي بالنسبة إلى الإنسان، وَكُلٌّ مِنْهُمَا، أي الخاصة والعرض العام، إِنِ امْتَنَعَ انْفِكَاكُهُ عَنِ الْمَعْرُوضِ فَلَازِمٌ، وَإِلَّا امتنع فَمُفَارِقٌ ، يَزُولُ بِسُرْعَةٍ، كحمرة الخجل ، أَوْ بُطْءٍ، كالعشق، أَوْ لَا يزول أصلا، كحركة الفلك. وهذا التقسيم في بادئ الرأي، وإلا فبناء على الأصول المبرهنة في الفلسفة المفارق لا يكون دائما ؛ لأن المعتبر في مفهوم اللازم امتناع الانفكاك ، مطلقا بالذات كان أو بالغير (ثُمَّ اللَّازِمُ إِمَّا أَنْ يَمْتَنِعَ انْفِكَاكُهُ عَنِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ مُطْلَقًا، سواء كانت الخارج أو في الذهن بِعِلَّةٍ، أَوْ ضَرُورَةِ ذاتية يُسَمَّى لَازِمَ الْمَاهِيَّةِ، فالوجود المطلق والإمكان ونظائرهما داخلة فيه، وقد يقال لما يقتضيه الماهية حال اختلاطها بالوجود، فالمذكورات خارجة ، أَوْ يمتنع انفكاكه بِالنَّظْرِ إِلَى أَحَدِ الْوُجُودَيْن ، خَارِجِيَّا أَوْ ذِهْنِيًّا وَيُسَمَّى الثَّاني، أي لازم الوجود الذهني مَعْقُولًا ثَانِيًا، كالقياسية، وقد مر تفصيله، وَالدَّوَامُ لَا يَخْلُو عَنْ لُزُومِ سَبَبِيٍّ ) ؛ فإنه إذا لم يجب لم يوجد ، على ما تقرر في الفلسفة.
A chapter on the five universals. The fifth investigation: General Accident. The fifth universal: General Accident, and it is the universal external (to the essence) predicated on diverse realities, like 'walker' relative to man. And each of them, i.e., the proprium and the general accident, if its separation from the subject is impossible, then it is necessary; and if not impossible, then it is separable: it departs quickly, like the redness of shyness, or slowly, like infatuation, or does not depart at all, like the motion of the celestial sphere. This division is at first glance; otherwise, based on demonstrated principles in philosophy, the separable is not always (separable) because what is considered in the concept of necessary is the impossibility of separation, absolutely, whether by essence or by another. Then the necessary: either its separation from the essence is absolutely impossible, whether in external existence or in the mind, due to a cause or essential necessity, and it is called necessary of the essence; so absolute existence, contingency, and their like are included in it. And it may be said for what the essence necessitates when mixed with existence, so the mentioned ones are excluded. Or its separation is impossible with respect to one of the two existences, external or mental, and it is called the second, i.e., necessary of mental existence, a secondary intelligible, like the categoricalness, and its detail has passed. And perpetuity is not free from causal necessity; for if it is not necessary, it would not exist, according to what is established in philosophy.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth universal, al-'arad al-'amm (general accident). It is a universal that is external to the essence and predicated on multiple different realities (e.g., 'walker' can be said of man and horse). Then it discusses the division of accidents (both proprium and general accident) into necessary (lazim) and separable (mufariq). If separation from the subject is impossible, it is necessary; if possible, it is separable, which may be quickly departing, slowly departing, or everlasting (like celestial motion). The author notes that this division is preliminary; philosophy holds that the separable is not always actually separable because the criterion for being necessary is impossibility of separation, whether due to essence or an external cause. Then the passage subdivides the necessary: first, the essential necessary (lazim al-mahiyya) which cannot be separated from the essence at all, whether in the external or mental realm, such as absolute existence and contingency. Some restrict it to what the essence requires when mixed with existence, excluding those. Second, the necessary with respect to one existence (external or mental), called the secondary intelligible (ma'qul thani), e.g., categoricalness. Finally, it notes that perpetuity (of an accident) requires causal necessity; otherwise, it would not exist. This demonstrates the ontological commitment of the logicians: even accidents considered 'necessary' are ultimately dependent on causes.

Key Terms
العرض العام
لازم
معقول ثاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a necessary accident (lazim) that is not separable from its subject?
A) Redness of shyness
B) Infatuation
C) Motion of the celestial sphere
D) Contingency for a created being

Key Takeaway
The general accident is a universal external to essence predicated on multiple realities; its necessity is defined by impossibility of separation, not by permanence, and necessary accidents are subdivided into essential and secondary types.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Common Accident: Definition and Division into Necessary and Separable
Author defines common accident and divides it with proper accident into necessary and separable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a common accident and classify it as necessary or separable based on the impossibility of separation.

Core Idea
The common accident is a universal applying to diverse realities; its necessity depends on inseparability from the subject.

The fifth universal in classical logic is the common accident. Unlike the proper accident which applies to only one species, the common accident applies across multiple realities. The author then divides both accidents into necessary and separable based on whether they can be removed from the subject. This division helps us understand the ontological status of attributes.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition of common accident
It is a universal predicated on different realities, like 'walking' that applies to both humans and animals.
2
Understand the criteria for necessary vs separable
If separation from the subject is impossible, it is necessary (lāzim); if possible, it is separable (mufāriq).
3
Note the author's philosophical caveat
The initial division is provisional; in reality, the separable cannot be perpetual because necessity is defined by impossibility of separation.
4
Recognize examples of separable
Quick: redness of bashfulness; slow: love; never: celestial motion (but actually necessary in reality).

فصل في الكليات الخمس
الْمَبْحَثُ الْخَامِسُ الْعَرَضُ الْعَامُ )
الكلي الْخَامِسُ : الْعَرَضُ الْعَامُّ ، وَهُوَ الكلي الْخَارِجُ الْمَقُولُ عَلَى حَقَائِقَ مُخْتَلِفَةٍ، كالماشي بالنسبة إلى الإنسان، وَكُلٌّ مِنْهُمَا، أي الخاصة والعرض العام، إِنِ امْتَنَعَ انْفِكَاكُهُ عَنِ الْمَعْرُوضِ فَلَازِمٌ، وَإِلَّا امتنع فَمُفَارِقٌ ، يَزُولُ بِسُرْعَةٍ، كحمرة الخجل ، أَوْ بُطْءٍ، كالعشق، أَوْ لَا يزول أصلا، كحركة الفلك. وهذا التقسيم في بادئ الرأي، وإلا فبناء على الأصول المبرهنة في الفلسفة المفارق لا يكون دائما ؛ لأن المعتبر في مفهوم اللازم امتناع الانفكاك ، مطلقا بالذات كان أو بالغير .
ثُمَّ اللَّازِمُ إِمَّا أَنْ يَمْتَنِعَ انْفِكَاكُهُ عَنِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ مُطْلَقًا، سواء كانت الخارج أو في الذهن بِعِلَّةٍ، أَوْ ضَرُورَةِ ذاتية يُسَمَّى لَازِمَ الْمَاهِيَّةِ، فالوجود المطلق والإمكان ونظائرهما داخلة فيه، وقد يقال لما يقتضيه الماهية حال اختلاطها بالوجود، فالمذكورات خارجة ، أَوْ يمتنع انفكاكه بِالنَّظْرِ إِلَى أَحَدِ الْوُجُودَيْن ، خَارِجِيَّا أَوْ ذِهْنِيًّا وَيُسَمَّى الثَّاني، أي لازم الوجود الذهني مَعْقُولًا ثَانِيًا، كالقياسية، وقد مر تفصيله، وَالدَّوَامُ لَا يَخْلُو عَنْ لُزُومِ سَبَبِيٍّ ؛ فإنه إذا لم يجب لم يوجد ، على ما تقرر في الفلسفة.
Chapter on the Five Universals. The fifth investigation: The Common Accident. The fifth universal: the common accident, and it is the universal that is predicated on different realities, like 'walking' in relation to man. And each of them (i.e., the proper accident and the common accident), if its separation from the subject is impossible, then it is necessary (lazim), and if not impossible, then it is separable (mufariq), which may disappear quickly, like the redness of bashfulness, or slowly, like love, or not at all, like the motion of the celestial sphere. This division is according to initial view; otherwise, based on established principles in philosophy, the separable is not perpetual; because what is considered in the concept of the necessary is the impossibility of separation, absolutely, whether by essence or by other. Then the necessary (lazim) is either such that its separation from the essence is impossible absolutely (whether in the external or in the mind) due to a cause or a self-evident necessity, and it is called the necessary of the essence (lazim al-mahiyya). So absolute existence, potentiality, and their like are included in it. And it may be said what the essence necessitates when it is mixed with existence, then the aforementioned are excluded. Or its separation is impossible with regard to one of the two existences, external or mental, and it is called the second, i.e., the necessary of mental existence, the secondary intelligible, like quiddity, and its detail has passed. And perpetuity is not free from a causal necessity; because if it is not necessary, it would not exist, as established in philosophy.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth universal, the common accident, and provides a detailed classification. The author first gives the definition: the common accident is a universal that applies to different realities, like 'walking' applicable to both man and horse. Then he divides it with the proper accident (the fourth universal) into either necessary (lazim) or separable (mufariq), depending on whether separation from the subject is impossible or not. The separable is further subdivided by speed of separation: quick (like blushing), slow (like love), or permanent (like celestial motion). However, the author notes this division is provisional; in reality, the separable cannot be permanent because necessity is defined by impossibility of separation, whether essential or accidental. Next, the necessary is split into two types: (1) necessary of the essence (lazim al-mahiyya), where separation is absolutely impossible due to a cause or self-evident necessity, including absolute existence and potentiality; (2) necessary of mental existence (lazim al-wujud al-dhihni), which is a secondary intelligible like quiddity. Finally, the author remarks that perpetuity always involves a causal necessity, as established in philosophy. This passage is foundational for understanding the classification of universals and the nature of predicables.

لازم
مفارق
